<span id="freeTextContainer2537552966250756525">This is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11979909.The_Girls_of_No_Return' title='The Girls of No Return by Erin Saldin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girls of No Return</a> meets <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17797364.And_We_Stay' title='And We Stay by Jenny Hubbard' rel='nofollow noopener'>And We Stay</a> in the best way possible. I love this story about <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ mental illness  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the power of literature, of words, of writing, and of believing in things you do and do not have control of. <br/><br/>My one criticism is that in the final two chapters -- the second-to-last especially -- Wolitzer gets too on-the-nose. It feels a bit rookie YA, explaining The Great Meaning Here to the readers who will have gotten it because they're smart e</span>
  <span id="freeText2537552966250756525" style="display:none">This is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11979909.The_Girls_of_No_Return" title="The Girls of No Return by Erin Saldin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girls of No Return</a> meets <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17797364.And_We_Stay" title="And We Stay by Jenny Hubbard" rel="nofollow noopener">And We Stay</a> in the best way possible. I love this story about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ mental illness  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the power of literature, of words, of writing, and of believing in things you do and do not have control of. <br /><br />My one criticism is that in the final two chapters -- the second-to-last especially -- Wolitzer gets too on-the-nose. It feels a bit rookie YA, explaining The Great Meaning Here to the readers who will have gotten it because they're smart enough. <br /><br />You don't need to be familiar with Plath or her book to get the story. Likewise, I would say this book walks the fine line of magical realism/contemporary realistic, depending on your interpretation of the events that unfold. <br /><br />The voice really drives this novel, and Jam's voice is compelling, her actions and decisions flawed, and her approaches to new relationships in her life consistent with what we know initially, as well as what we learn about her as the story goes.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I won't lie. I called the story's "twist" near immediately, but it didn't at all change my feelings about it. I did look for evidence to support my theory, but I didn't at all feel cheated when I was correct in my assumptions. I think I've just read more than most when it comes to mental health in YA fiction.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Longer review to come. </span>

  <span id="freeText9966724739468181578" style="display:none">I received an ARC from Netgalley.<br /><br />I can't believe this is written by the same woman who wrote The Interestings. The character development in Belzhar is - well, there isn't any. I felt no attachment to any of the characters. They are poorly drawn and have no depth. The dialogue - where do I begin? It's one of my favorite books because of the character development. Maybe YA just isn't Wolitzer's genre.</span>

<div id="review_1946383552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946383552" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537582300p2/33012180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946383552?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21793400-belzhar">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012180-chelsea?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946383552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12460909561186442376">I picked this book up in an airport over two years ago, never having heard of it. I instantly started it, and while I loved the writing style I remember having rather mixed feelings. I decided to revisit it to see whether I wanted to keep it or unhaul it (since it is only a three star I settled on unhaul, though it does have lots of things I like about it).<br/><br/>This follows a teenage girl named Jam Gallahue. After her boyfriend dies, Jam is utterly distraught. Her parents decide to send her to a boar</span>
  <span id="freeText12460909561186442376" style="display:none">I picked this book up in an airport over two years ago, never having heard of it. I instantly started it, and while I loved the writing style I remember having rather mixed feelings. I decided to revisit it to see whether I wanted to keep it or unhaul it (since it is only a three star I settled on unhaul, though it does have lots of things I like about it).<br /><br />This follows a teenage girl named Jam Gallahue. After her boyfriend dies, Jam is utterly distraught. Her parents decide to send her to a boarding school called The Wooden Barn for kids dealing with trauma.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I’ve now compared Reeve Maxfield to both math and chemistry. But in the end the only class that came to matter in all of this was English...it was the one I took much later, at The Wooden Barn up in Vermont, after Reeve was gone and I could barely live.”</i>
</blockquote><br />There, Jam is surprised to learn she has been chosen for the prestigious and mysterious class called Special Topics in English. There, the students study Sylvia Plath and receive journals that are not just ordinary journals.<br /><br />Plotwise, it’s an interesting novel. <b>I love stories with a ragtag group of people with different backgrounds being thrust together, which instantly drew me to this book.</b><br /><br />I won’t go into spoilers, but this one of those books that has a lot of mystery within it and a huge plot twist, one I did not think served to strengthen the story.<br /><br /><b>The writing is absolutely my favorite part of this book.</b> The style is one that makes everything seem important, and it has a strong narrative voice and character descriptions.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“We each have only one voice...and the world is so loud. Sometimes I think that the quiet ones...have figured out that the best way to get other people’s attention is not to shout, but to whisper. Which makes everyone listen a little harder.”</i>
</blockquote><br />As far as the characters go, they were interesting, but I never felt like we got to see beyond a few distinct traits of theirs. Jam’s obsession with describing her old boyfriend was incredibly tedious.<br /><br /><b>This is also a book that feels it’s length, which in this case is quite short. At times it felt rushed, especially with way the characters relationships developed.</b> Like Jam just seemed to suddenly be friends with certain people without seeing what led up to it.<br /><br />Overall, I’m glad I took the time to reread this one and sort out my feelings. <b>This is a book that has great writing and is easy to discuss, but could have used some work to create a more cohesive story.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12460909561186442376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1037331923" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1037331923" />
    <a title="Jamie (The Perpetual Page-Turner)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1518370-jamie-the-perpetual-page-turner"><img alt="Jamie (The Perpetual Page-Turner)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453742375p2/1518370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1037331923?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie (The Perpetual Page-Turner)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie (The Perpetual Page-Turner)" href="/user/show/1518370-jamie-the-perpetual-page-turner">Jamie (The Perpetual Page-Turner)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1518370-jamie-the-perpetual-page-turner?shelf=for-review-physical-copy">for-review-physical-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1037331923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14415827264868602711"><br/>I talked more personally about this book on my blog, The Perpetual Page-Turner, and how The Bell Jar was important to me and about how this kind of took me back to a time in my life that was hard. So if you want to read THAT...<a href='http://www.perpetualpageturner.com/2014/09/but-theres-always-something-else-at-the-end.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>go here</a>! But I wanted to actually let you know more what I thought about it here!<br/><br/>What I Liked:<br/><br/>1. The plot -- it was super interesting! A girl whose boyfriend dies and she isn't handling it well at all gets sent to a special school with other kids who have some issues and n</span>
  <span id="freeText14415827264868602711" style="display:none"><br />I talked more personally about this book on my blog, The Perpetual Page-Turner, and how The Bell Jar was important to me and about how this kind of took me back to a time in my life that was hard. So if you want to read THAT...<a href="http://www.perpetualpageturner.com/2014/09/but-theres-always-something-else-at-the-end.html" rel="nofollow noopener">go here</a>! But I wanted to actually let you know more what I thought about it here!<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />1. The plot -- it was super interesting! A girl whose boyfriend dies and she isn't handling it well at all gets sent to a special school with other kids who have some issues and needs therapy. She gets put into this mysterious English class that is super hard to get into and nobody even KNOWS how you get picked to be in it. They study the works of Sylvia Plath the whole semester and are given a journal they HAVE to write in. And what happens with the journal I'm not telling you! I was VERY much engaged and interested!<br /><br />2. So quoteable: I can't tell you how many dog-ears I made with just really great lines or passages. The writing was pretty solid and it was very thought-provoking!<br /><br />3. I thought I had this book's number but NOPE -- I thought I knew the trajectory of the story pretty much and let me tell you...it took me for a bit of a ride. I didn't see something coming and how it was revealed and built-up to was SMART.<br /><br />4. Some of the characters and their stories were intriguing! I really liked our main character and some of the friends she made. I LOVED how their group came together and supported each other. I wish we would have seen a LITTLE more of the teacher because she intrigued me a whole lot.<br /><br /><br />What I Didn't Like:<br /><br />1. The pacing wasn't consistent -- there were times I was racing to read this and there were other times it just was DRAGGING and DRAGGING. Too much in some places, not enough in others.<br /><br />2. Way too "this is the message/lesson" -- This was a really thought-provoking novel! However, it felt almost as the author didn't quite trust the reader to glean some of the important things out of it. At the end it was super THIS IS THE MESSAGE and I felt like it was dumping it all out there to make sure I got it. Which I did.<br /><br />3. Sometimes I felt we were being TOLD stuff rather than shown -- There were certain areas where I think I was supposed to feel more but instead I felt like it was just being told to me and I was like okay so this is happening. Like instead of FEELING changed attitudes and hearts..I was just told that there were changes.<br /><br /><br /><br />Overall, Belzhar was enjoyable and engaging. It wasn't always consistent but at its highs it was GREAT. It felt unique and I loved how thought-provoking it was. In certain ways I think this could have been better but I did like it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14415827264868602711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2728652201" />
    <a title="Jay G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30890847-jay-g"><img alt="Jay G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505302632p2/30890847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2728652201?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay G" href="/user/show/30890847-jay-g">Jay G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142426296" href="/book/show/25310585-belzhar">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2728652201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11906276554726605156">Want to see more bookish things from me? Check out my youtube channel: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCferU-BCL2dlFjWdD0rS75Q'>https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCfer...</a><br/><br/>3.5/5 Stars <br/><br/>After being unable to cope with the death of her boyfriend Reeve Maxfield, Jam Gallahue is sent to the Wooden Barn, a boarding school for troubled teens. Upon arriving, Jam is chosen to be apart of a class called Special Topics in English that is invite only. When Mrs. Q assigns their first journaling assignment and Jam begins to write in the red leather notebook provided, s</span>
  <span id="freeText11906276554726605156" style="display:none">Want to see more bookish things from me? Check out my youtube channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCferU-BCL2dlFjWdD0rS75Q">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCfer...</a><br /><br />3.5/5 Stars <br /><br />After being unable to cope with the death of her boyfriend Reeve Maxfield, Jam Gallahue is sent to the Wooden Barn, a boarding school for troubled teens. Upon arriving, Jam is chosen to be apart of a class called Special Topics in English that is invite only. When Mrs. Q assigns their first journaling assignment and Jam begins to write in the red leather notebook provided, she is transported to Belzhar, an alternate universe where she can be with Reeve once again. <br /><br />I really enjoyed learning each teenagers backstory and why they ended up at The Wooden Barn in the first place. I did find Jam's fixation on Reeve to be a bit stupid, as they had only known each other for 41 days before she fell into this deep depression over him. Honestly I was more interested in the side characters than I was in Jam and her story. I loved the idea of Belzhar and was intrigued with how the whole process/world worked but I wasn't fully invested in Jam and her story.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1348490249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1348490249" />
    <a title="Izzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31211197-izzy"><img alt="Izzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593145096p2/31211197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1348490249?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Izzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Izzy" href="/user/show/31211197-izzy">Izzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1348490249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4334785382824476848"><i>
  <blockquote>"It's funny how you can go for a long time in life not needing someone, and then you meet them and you suddenly need them all the time."</blockquote>
</i><br/>If <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History' title='The Secret History by Donna Tartt' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Secret History</a> had an annoying little sister going through an emo phase, it would be <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821376.Belzhar' title='Belzhar by Meg Wolitzer' rel='nofollow noopener'> Belzhar</a>.<br/><br/>Jamaica is a sixteen years old girl who's been moping around in her bedroom for the past year because her boyfriend, Reeve, died. They spent exactly forty one days together and they were crazy in love and now Jam feels that she can't go on with her life beca</span>
  <span id="freeText4334785382824476848" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"It's funny how you can go for a long time in life not needing someone, and then you meet them and you suddenly need them all the time."</blockquote>
</i><br />If <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Secret History</a> had an annoying little sister going through an emo phase, it would be <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821376.Belzhar" title="Belzhar by Meg Wolitzer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Belzhar</a>.<br /><br />Jamaica is a sixteen years old girl who's been moping around in her bedroom for the past year because her boyfriend, Reeve, died. They spent exactly forty one days together and they were crazy in love and now Jam feels that she can't go on with her life because Reeve has passed away, so her parents sent her to a boarding school in Vermont that deals with "fragile" (ugh) teenagers to see if she can get better. There, she and four other students are selected to participate in a special English class that allegedly changed the lives of everyone who's involved with it.<br /><br />Normally, this is the kind of book I'd love. It has brooding, troubled teenagers, characters with deep dark secrets, and a very similar premise to TSH, which I <i>loved</i>. But from the very start I wasn't really feeling this. Jam is plain and annoying. She was very bitchy to everyone around her, including her little brother who did literally nothing to her other than, y'know, care about her well-being, and she kept coming off as nothing more than a spoiled teenage girl going through a very bad emo phase. I mean, seriously:<br /><i>
  <blockquote>"In a way, the darkness suits me; it suits my mood tonight and every night."</blockquote>
</i><br />That's EXACTLY the kind of thing I would've written when I was thirteen and listening to Simple Plan's <i>Perfect</i> very loudly in my room because I was so deep and dark and no one else could understand me.<br /><br />I enjoyed the author's writing style for the most part, though, and the way she described scenes and places throughout the book and the side character's stories <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(particularly Sierra's, because I'm such a sap and everything that involves siblings and their dynamics touches me in a very personal way) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were the only reason I didn't stop reading this book a long time ago.<br /><br />One thing that I didn't enjoy in the slightest was how a lot of things that happened in the story weren't actually included in the book. For example, around the middle of the book Jam starts saying she and Sierra became super close and how they're best friends and have had a lot of these meaningful conversations, but we never actually <i>see</i> any of it happening. We barely see them interacting out of class! It's like the author was too tired to write everything and thought that just briefly mentioning it happened afterwards would be okay.<br /><br />Jam is also surprinsigly good at everything she tries. She joins an acapella group out of the blue in school, but of course her voice is clear and good so she has nothing to worry about! She tries cross-country skiing for the first time and it turns out to be so easy! She spends the entire book saying how terrible she was at math but suddenly all the exercises make sense and she gets them all right! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She helps Mr. Fowley deliver a freaking baby goat perfectly! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I won't get much into it, because I think that if I do I'd never shut up about it, but the twist did nothing for me other than make me MAJORLY pissed off. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You throw her in the midst of people who have gone through real, severe traumas - one has a missing brother, the other can't walk because her mom crashed their car, the other started a fire and killed a bunch of goats, and the other one tore his family apart - just to tell us moments before the books ends that she imagined all of it??? And she's just a spoiled girl with an obsessive personality who couldn't get over the fact that the guy she wanted to be with was just not that into her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In the end, I realized that sticking through the book wasn't worth it at all, because all I felt at the end was disappointment and rage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4334785382824476848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('o8MM6Y8SgvGXFD4hIKcbZSGJSCqmH6PWFkNes4sag3B0ZeUyAPW6yT/eZ/oxDV97oeQKrlFDdaqQ7NvLmQUnOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z/0+rihC2+fBoZwQmuaIdPZxLEprmc+fW+obz74tGbSwW9d1p6Xj32lrxcuLTMxqdhxuzpzFGePdRZ63rDK9/g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

The world’s first superstar, she traveled with a chimpanzee named Darwin and a pet alligator that drank champagne, shamelessly supplementing her income by endorsing everything from aperitifs to beef bouillon, and spreading rumors that she slept in a coffin to better understand the macabre heroines she played. Eleonora Duse shied away from the spotlight. Born to a penniless family of itinerant troubadours, she disappeared into the characters she portrayed—channeling their spirits, she claimed. Her new, empathetic style of acting revolutionized the theater—and earned her the ire of Sarah Bernhardt in what would become the most tumultuous theatrical showdown of the nineteenth century. Bernhardt and Duse seduced each other’s lovers, stole one another’s favorite playwrights, and took to the world’s stages to outperform their rival in her most iconic roles. A scandalous, enormously entertaining history full of high drama and low blows, Playing to the Gods is the page-turning account of the feud that changed theater forever.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12610593636923695993">Meg Wolitzer is the <i>New York Times</i>–bestselling author of <i>The Interestings, The Uncoupling, The Ten-Year Nap, The Position, The Wife</i>, and <i>Sleepwalking</i>. She is also the author of the young adult novel <i>Belzhar</i>. Wolitzer lives in New York City.</span>
